Our pricing is up to date with current market trends when comparing top Power equipment Dealers and in some cases we are actually too low. We also do not run a cash only, cash wages, no insurance, avoid paying taxes business and never will.  We also have many expenses to running a successful business of our type that you may be unfamiliar with such as manufacturer training, software licenses, department of weights and measures, Hazardous waste generation permits, and the list goes on and on, so being the "cheapest" will probably not happen, but we will charge a fair market rate that will assure we can stay in business for many more years.\nOur hours of operation are adjusted to work around the 95% of our customer base which is primarily made up of professional landscapers, municipalities, contractors and school districts. < Review>
I cant believe how accommodating and understanding the social workers/case workers here are. It was my first time applying for any type of help for my son and I ever, and was unclear of the process. I had a 'in-home visit' which I'd failed to be home for, and wasn't able to cancel prior to, or even reachable. Something very important had suddenly come up and they couldn't locate or contact me for a week, maybe more. You'd think I would have understandably been dropped from CalWorks immediately. Instead, they tried very hard contact me daily. Finally when they did, and after providing proof of my whereabouts/sudden emergency, EVERYONE was more than understanding. My social worker Victoria, who called me relentlessly, Fatima-my case worker, and her supervisor-unfortunately, never got her name-all helped me out more than I could have even hoped for. I'd put everyone on my case through some confusion and they never held any of it against me and I was always treated with all the respect.
My experience with "social workers'' hasnt always been pleasant and was nervous to ask for help. But this place isn't like that. So, if you are like me, dont be afraid to come here and get the help if you need it. These people are actually willing and here to help.

Edit: Feel I have to share again since my last post 5 months ago. Once again, another great experience. What I tried accomplishing at another office 2 different times and days, yet werent able to.. we were able to resolve in less than 1 hr here at this location..Every worker I've come across here has been amazing!<//Review>

< text>
I sure did not expect to give Presto Grill such a low rating. But I must because overall the food was not good.

The restaurant is clean and inviting. You can sit outside on the spacious patio or inside at one of the small tables. All unexpected in the middle of the Fabric District. The waitress and cooks were nice and friendly. Service was fast. Prices were good.

The koubideh was not good. The flavor of the meat and the seasonings were bad. It tasted like they had mixed liver in with the meat when it was ground. That is not necessarily bad but in this case was way too much and affected the flavor overall.

I had the Zeresk polo and boneless chicken. It was good. The zeresk were not too sweet and not too sour. The chicken was cooked perfectly. This is hard to find as many places cut the pieces uneven
And they cook unevenly on the grill. So perfect Chicken and zeresk polo.

We took a Falafel sandwich to go. How could they make it bad? I really wanted it to be good. It came with French fries which were great. The French roll was perfect for a sandwich. Onions, pickles and lettuce were very tasty but the falafel was just bad. It didn't taste good at all. I couldn't even eat it.
I was so sad because the bread had so much potential.

Should be 2.5 Stars.<//text>

<Text>Good food. The outdoor seating gives you a good view of the busy street and the ambience of the Los Angeles life. The restroom is clean with neatly placed ornaments, the smell is floral and the floor is dry.
However, even though the outdoor seating a good choice because of the view and the ambience, if you don't like to smell of cigarette smoke, better use the indoor seating. On the inside seating, you'll be treated with a background music of the piped in music (it was Richard Clayderman album that was playing as shown on their wall TV)  and the conversation of the cook, and the flickering shadow of their ceiling fan.
Four 4-seater, three 2-seater tables inside and one 4-seater, four 2-seater tables outdoor.

< Text>
The food was decent and portion size left something to be desired... my friends & I ordered according to what the owner suggested as he said they didn't have several items that are pictured on their wall. My vegetarian platter had a large salad but it was mostly the white part of the iceberg lettuce and not very many greens. Instead of falafel they tossed a chopped up veggie burger that was purchased from Costco which I also have in my freezer at home. My friends had similar salad platters one with tiny pieces of chicken sprinkled on the top & the other with one skinny kebab. The presentation was nice & we enjoyed our meals until the verbal total was announced. We were shocked to hear our total was $41.00 for our 3 dishes when most of their dishes are advised here for $6.99!!! Not at all what we expect from a hole in the wall diner style restaurant on the east side of DTLA. When we asked for separate checks & the owner didn't want to split them up... we were the only people there so it wasn't like it was an inconvenience. I was going to pay with credit card & have my friends give me cash but then he said their credit card machine wasn't activated yet as they were under new ownership as of 3 weeks ago. When we asked for a break down of the prices he explained that the chicken was an extra $3 & the sides of tahini & hummus that we didn't order were $2 each... he brought them with the platters so naturally we assumed that came with it. We never saw an actual bill & because the items on their printed menu as well as their picture menu on their wall were entirely  different he could just charge what ever he wants. I would have never sat down if I had know I was going to pay $14 for a mediocre veggie salad & soda!!  I paid $6 for a similar platter from here that had these fantastic giant falafel balls & was the reason I came back with my friends. Funny thing is the previous owner was sitting inside the whole time & when I asked if he knew the previous owner he said it was the lady inside who had come by to get some mail.  I'm all about supporting my local businesses & keeping it in the family but I don't appreciate being lied to my face & haggling over prices... we won't be coming back here again unless his mom decides to do a free falafel day!</Text>

< Review>
Fairly easy to moderate hike if you begin immediately to the right as soon as you see the creeks at entrance. You can either go up the creek or follow a tiny trail alongside it. Not much water but the sight is beautiful. You can then go up the steep climb using a rope for other interesting trails to the top. Your shoes need to be hiking for better support. If you take the other main trail closest to the creek there‚Äôs the steep climb down to the falls, I believe could be dangerous and higher risk for slipping. Know your limitations as your safety should always be top priority. Be careful with poison oak as well</Review>

Mimi Wahinee< /Name>
< Review>
The hike is fairly easy for a any hiker. There wasn‚Äôt much water so there wasn‚Äôt any water falls but still worth going. To get to the falls, if you‚Äôre going during a fairly dry season, I suggest walking through the creek. It‚Äôll require some climbing over boulders but nothing difficult. It‚Äôs such an amazing hike from below as opposed to the top trail. It‚Äôs the way less taken. So you can enjoy a nice quiet walk in nature.

Once you get to the ‚Äúpool‚Äù you can climb on one of those rocks to get a different vantage point and see the other ‚Äúpools‚Äù. I was there by myself and it was amazing.

To get back, I suggest going up the path (where the trail would take you down). There‚Äôs a rope that you can use to get on the top trail. Then hike the trail down. It goes down from there, so that should make it easier.< /Review>

One of the best hikes I've had. Mission Creek is energizing and beautiful. If you have it in you follow the creek upwards and you will come across more waterfalls. I started at Inspiration Point Trailhead and followed Mission Creek upwards. Sometimes you have to go around the creek because of the lack of access. I would grade the hike moderate to challenging.< /review>

<Text>Customer service 8/10 -little pushy

Timeliness 3/10 -took way too long

Quality 3/10 -missed a lot of areas and flat out didn't clean other areas.

Also upon inspection (I have rain guards on my windows) the guy who cleaned my car didn't even roll down the windows so once the car was dried there was about 2.5inches on every window of dirt at the top. <review>This is specifically for the Soquel Avenue location. This is one of the best taquerias in town and I'm always amazed that it doesn't make the "best of" lists published. The carna asada has SO much flavor. The tacos are delicious and packed full of meat. I'd highly recommend the carne asada tacos, any variety of the super burritos (but especially the shrimp), the cheese enchiladas, and the tostado. Prices are fairly reasonable, but they've gone up lately. Parking is easy to find and the restaurant itself is huge with plenty of tables. They have a salsa bar with amazing pico de gayo and serve fresh chips with every order. There's a selection of Mexican beverages and desserts. The interior is a little worn, and some menu items are pricier than others. Really love this place.<//review><gmap_id>0x808e401f20b179af:0xc63f5a798f88d436</gmap_id><Rate>4< /Rate>< Time>

<Rate>3< /Rate><review>Reading these reviews I have come to the following conclusions:
1. This place has excellent tacos. Order them.
2. Get the Al Pastor as your meat choice.
3. Don't order veggie here. (Or at any taqueria really. I mean c'mon.)
4. If you're acting privileged you will be treated accordingly. Smile and be respectful.
5. Be prepared to spend a little more than you'd like, but the Al Pastor tacos will make you glad you did.
6. If all else fails order the soup. The soup is the best thing on the menu.
7. Whatever you order get it to go, make sure to check it over before you leave, like any thinking person would.
Enjoy!< /review><pics>None<//pics><Response>None<//Response><Gmap_id>0x808e401f20b179af:0xc63f5a798f88d436< /Gmap_id></record>

< text>
The service can be a little surly and gruff, but the food is fantastic. Taqueria Santa Cruz has some favorites that you just can't get in other taquerias, like birria (bbq goat), carne en su jugo (beef soup), and camarones en mojo de ajo (shrimp in garlic sauce). They could be a little less stingy with their chips (you only get a tiny bag with your meal) but their salsas are delicious.</text>

<GmapID>0x808e401f20b179af:0xc63f5a798f88d436<//GmapID><Response>None<//Response>< text>
Lackluster service, worst vegetarian burrito I have ever had, inflated prices, gossipy environment and last time I went I found a pebble in my burrito. They replaced it but the new burrito was mostly inedible.

To be more clear, my second or third time coming to this restaurant, the woman at the cash register, who was already very unfriendly, got angry because I asked a man behind me for change so I wouldn't have to break my last twenty. He was more than happy to supply the change but she acted like I was pan handling and told me if I ever do that again she would kick me out and I would be persona non grata. I made a review highlighting her treatment of me that day, as well as previous times where her attitude was equally unkind.

I made the mistake of going in one final time after a late night work out. I ordered the tripas burrito. I tried to be friendly and ask her how she was and I honestly asked if she had seen my review. She said she had.  I was feeling incredibly gracious and even apologized for posting it. She said it was fine and that people were even coming in telling her how great she was because of it. I was genuinely happy she was able to receive positively because of my review.

I left with my daughter and I' s food. I got inside my vehicle, took a bite and bit down on a huge pebble, and what appeared to be pieces of rocks. I brought back the burrito and asked her sincerely if it was retribution for the review I wrote. She said she was insulted by my inquiry. She said that it was normal for tripas burritos to have pebbles in them. She refused to refund my money and offered a replacement burrito.

Again, I made the mistake of going along instead of insisting on a refund. This time I chose a vegetarian burrito, hoping it would be pebble free. I even kept glancing at the guys making it. It was the worst burrito I had ever tasted. Maybe some folks like feta and lettuce galore in their burrito but not me! It got tossed, even though I normally don't waste food.

As an empath and  single mom of three, I feel everything deeply. Kindness and lack thereof. In a way, the unkindness serves me too, because it has taught me deep, tearful  gratitide for kindness and people who choose kindness. This place has taught me deep gratitude for good food (pebble free), good service, and of course, kindness. May we all choose more and more kindness, especially since we all depend on it.

I hope this helps and thank you for reading.< /text>
